		1.2.9
	1.3 IPV6


		1.3.1  Development Environment

			1.3.1.1  ISATAP 
from wikipedia:
			(Intra-Site Automatic Tunnel Addressing Protocol) is an IPv6 transition mechanism meant to transmit IPv6 packets between dual-stack nodes on top of an IPv4 network.

Unlike 6over4 (an older similar protocol using IPv4 multicast), ISATAP uses IPv4 as a virtual nonbroadcast multiple-access network (NBMA) data link layer, so that it does not require the underlying IPv4 network infrastructure to support multicast.
Contents
 [hide] 

|    1 How ISATAP works
|        1.1 Link-local address generation
|        1.2 Neighbor Discovery
|    2 Criticisms of ISATAP
|    3 Implementations of ISATAP
|    4 References
|    5 Other
|    6 External links

 How ISATAP works

ISATAP defines a method for generating a link-local IPv6 address from an IPv4 address, and a mechanism to perform Neighbor Discovery on top of IPv4.
 Link-local address generation

Any host wishing to participate in ISATAP over a given IPv4 network can set up a virtual IPv6 network interface. The link-local address is determined by concatenating fe80:0000:0000:0000:0200:5efe: for global unique and fe80:0000:0000:0000:0000:5efe: for private addresses with the 32 bits of the host's IPv4 address.

For example, host 192.0.2.143 would use fe80:0000:0000:0000:0200:5efe:"192.0.2.143" as its link-local IPv6 address. A shortened notation would be fe80::200:5efe:c000:028f (192.0.2.143 is c000028f in hexadecimal notation).
 Neighbor Discovery

Because ISATAP uses IPv4 as a non multicast/broadcast-capable (unlike Ethernet) link layer, ICMPv6 Neighbor Discovery cannot be done in the usual manner. That is why ISATAP is a bit more complex than 6over4.

The link layer address associated with a given IPv6 address is contained in the lower-order 32-bits of the IPv6 address, so that Neighbor Discovery is not really needed. However, the lack of multicast support prevents the use of automatic Router Discovery. Therefore, ISATAP hosts must be configured with a potential routers list (PRL). Each of these routers is infrequently probed by an ICMPv6 Router Discovery message, to determine which of them are functioning, and to perform unicast-only autoconfiguration (typically, obtain the list of on-link IPv6 prefixes that can be used).

In practice, implementations build their PRL by querying the DNS, e.g. by looking up isatap.example.com if the local domain is example.com. The local domain is typically obtained via DHCP (over IPv4) or statically configured.
 Criticisms of ISATAP

ISATAP typically builds its PRL by consulting the DNS; hence, it is a lower-layer protocol that relies on a higher layer. A circularity is avoided by relying on an IPv4 DNS server, which does not rely on IPv6 routing being established; however, this is a violation of network design principles, and feels brittle to some network specialists.[1]

ISATAP carries the same security risks as 6over4: the IPv4 virtual link must be delimited carefully at the network edge, so that external IPv4 hosts cannot pretend to be part of the ISATAP link. That is normally done by ensuring that proto-41 cannot pass through the firewall.
 Implementations of ISATAP

ISATAP is implemented in Microsoft Windows XP, Windows Vista, Windows 7, Windows Mobile, Linux, and in some versions of Cisco IOS.

Due to a patent claim, early in-kernel implementations were withdrawn from both KAME (*BSD) and USAGI (Linux). However the IETF IPR disclosure search engine reports that the would-be infringing patent’s holder requires no license from implementers.[2] ISATAP support has been supported in Linux since kernel version 2.6.25,[3] the tool isatapd [notes 1] provides a userspace helper. For prior kernels, the open source project Miredo provided an incomplete userland ISATAP implementation, which was removed in version 1.1.6.

			1.3.1.2 ISATAP End-User Instructions (http://wikicentral.cisco.com/display/IPV6NDCS/ISATAP+End-User+Instructions )


During the period when IT is ramping up its management tools, enabling IPv6 on the desktop will be on a 'business need' basis. By default, systems managed by IT will have IPv6 disabled, but there will not be an active effort to keep them that way. If someone has a business need for IPv6 it can be enabled even on IT managed systems. That said, the IPv6 functionality itself will be handled on a community supported basis for the foreseeable future. Community support should be accessible via the mail lists:

    ipv6-interest
    non-standard-support-trolls
    mac-trolls

The most current configuration information will be maintained at the NDCS & CSPO IPv6 wiki page

In keeping with other community supported efforts, pointers to that site's current configuration information will also be available via:

    http://pc-wiki.cisco.com
    http://mac-wiki.cisco.com

The issue with the regional routers has been resolved, so please use the one you believe is closest to you. Note that at this time all external IPv6 traffic is routed via San Jose. The external connections will evolve as time and budgets permit.
Initial Instructions.

There will be an IT operated IPv6-over-IPv4 tunnel facility that uses the stateless encapsulation defined in RFC 5214 (isatap). This would normally be an automatic function for Windows systems with their IPv6 stack enabled. In order to initially limit usage to those with 'business need', the automated access will be inhibited requiring explicit end user action to make it work. This explicit action step will take the form of removing the name isatap.cisco.com from dns, which in turn requires the end user to create a host file entry for that on each local system that has business need for IPv6. The rest of the process and functionality remain unaffected, so as soon as the stack is on and the name resolves, IPv6 packets will start flowing.
The actual hosts file entry points to an IPv4 anycast address which will connect to the nearest tunnel endpoint within each region. The location of the hosts file is /etc/hosts for unix & OS X, and \windows\system32\drivers\etc\hosts for Windows systems. Any existing file is likely marked read-only, so after opening it with your favorite text editor paste in the following text, save it to your desktop, then after making sure there is no .txt extension (file name is hosts. ; NOT hosts.txt) fix any r/o and/or permissions issues then copy the file to the location appropriate for your system.
# isatap.cisco.com - anycast IPv4 address
# should be in the form:    address  <tab>  fqdn
| 171.69.7.186    isatap.legacy.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.sjc1.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.sjc2.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.rtp1.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.rtp2.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.syd1.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.syd2.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.bgl1.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.bgl2.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.ams1.cisco.com
| 171.69.10.1 isatap.ams2.cisco.com
XP / Server2003

The IPv6 stack on these systems is OFF by default. To enable it, open a Command window.
C:\> netsh
C:\> netsh> interface ipv6
C:\> netsh interface ipv6> install

this will run for a little while... ^c or exit/exit/exit once it has completed.
It is self-configuring so skip to Windows general below.


Vista / Server2008 / W7
Click here to re-enable the IPv6 Stack for Win7

The IPv6 stack on these systems is ON by default, though it may have been disabled if it is an IT managed system. To enable it if it is not already on click sequence :
Control Panel / Network & Sharing / Adapter Settings / select the physical interface
/ right-click / Properties / check the IPv6 box

If there is no IPv6 box :
Control Panel / Network & Sharing / Adapter Settings / select the physical interface
/ right-click / Properties / Install ... / Protocol / Add... / IPv6.

It is self configuring so skip to Windows general below.


Windows general

If the hosts file has been updated as above, ping the name isatap.cisco.com. Assuming that works, within 30 seconds there should be a tunnel interface configured with an IPv6 address in the range 2001:420:: . The exact prefix is the result of a conversation between the local stack and the nearest isatap router, so if the IPv4 ping failed the only IPv6 address on the isatap interface will be link local (the fe80:: range). Once there is a 2001:420:: address on the isatap interface ping 2001:4860:800d::6a (ipv6.google.com) and the system should be good to go.

Some people have noticed that you could avoid the need to update the hostfile by simply putting the IPv4 anycast address in via the netsh interface.
netsh interface ipv6 isatap set router 171.69.10.1

While that technically does the same thing as the hostfile entry, it might make diagnostics difficult later when the end user has forgotten they did that. If IT were to change the IPv4 address of the isatap routers, by using the netsh path a ping to the name isatap.cisco.com would work, while the actual isatap interface would never come up. By using the hostfile path, a ping to the name would fail consistently with the interface whenever IT changed the IPv4 address, and expose the fact that the local system was still resolving to the old address.

Another point raised is that the isatap interface doesn't always come up as quickly as expected, so people recommend to others that a reboot is the fix. While the reboot process does cause a delay and slow down the impatient, a better choice would be to force the stack to retry rather than waiting for its timer. This can be done by causing a reconnect event, either disconnecting the adapter or using the control panel path to disable and re-enable the interface.  Bouncing the interface has the same impact on initiating the isatap sequence, without having to shutdown everything else and restart.
Ubuntu

Simple setup described at  http://wwwin-blogs.cisco.com/dannhowa/entry/easy_peasy_ipv6_on_ubuntu
OS X

The IPv6 stack on these systems is ON by default but there is no isatap functionality built in. If you find the stack has has been turned off :
System Preferences / Network Settings
select the interface / Advanced / Configure IPv6 -> Auto

The following script will enable and automatically test a pseudo isatap functionality for OS X (or other *nix with appropriate adjustment of the interface names) by creating a local IPv6 address that works with the stateless encapsulation used by the isatap router. It is not a full function isatap interface (see intro comments for more), but will allow OS X nodes on the corporate network to acquire functional IPv6 access with a minimum of effort on your part. If you are unsure of the state due to sleep mode, delete first.
Usage: sudo ./pseudo_isatap.sh add | del en0 | en1 (region.)cisco.com (test)

Regions included in the conf file: SJC1 SJC2 RTP1 RTP2 AMS1 AMS2 SYD1 SYD2 BGL1 BGL2 Legacy
Test Script
#!/bin/bash
#######################################################################
# create pseudo 'isatap' interface via gif0 ipv6 over ipv4 tunnel
#######################################################################
#
#  This script sets up a pseudo isatap functionality for OS X.
#  A real isatap implementation would treat the local IPv4 network as
#  a common NBMA layer 2 segment, where all nodes sharing an IPv6
#  prefix would be considered on-link and therefore directly accessible.
#  This script **ONLY** sets up a tunnel interface to the local isatap
#  router, with a default IPv6 route through it. As a result, connectivity
#  will be limited to other pseudo_isatap nodes, and anything external
#  to the isatap router prefix.
#
#
#  Change log
#  Ver    1.0    Tony Hain    9/23/2010    Initial pass
#    1.1    Tony Hain    9/23/2010    Fix typo's in echo & comments
#                        moved Delete test to top to deal with /
#                          being on a different network when run
#                        added 'test' command option
#                        added known isatap prefix if/elif test
#    1.2    Tony Hain    10/1/2010    added support for Anyconnect
#                        added cisco internal IPv6 routes
#    1.3    Tony Hain    11/1/2010    added support for /etc/hosts
#                        added cisco internal regional isatap prefixes
#    1.4    Tony Hain    12/21/2010    added support for "legacy" router
#    1.5    Jeff R. Allen    03/01/2011    minor usability improvements
#    1.6    Tony Hain    3/4/2011    move prefixes to config file
#                        fix fqdn including 'isatap' & short name
#    1.7    Tony Hain    4/22/2011    bug fix in input parser
#
#
#
#######################################################################
#
# Open config file
#
eof=0
FILE="pseudo_isatap.conf"
declare -a ARRAY
count=0
#
if [ ! -f $FILE ]; then
    echo "Config file $FILE does not exist"
    echo "$FILE format: region prefix /len"
    exit 1
elif [ ! -r $FILE ]; then
    echo "Config file $FILE can not be read"
    exit 1
fi
exec 42<$FILE
    while [ $eof -eq 0 ];  do
        if read input_line <&42; then
           if [ "$input_line" != "" ]; then
            ARRAY[$count]=$input_line
            ((count++))
           fi
        else
            eof=1
        fi
    done
exec 42>&-
 
#
#  syntax check
if [ "$1" = "-h" ] || [ "$3" = "" ] ; then
   echo "Usage:  sudo ./pseudo_isatap.sh   add | del   en0 | en1 | utun0    (region.)example.com   (test)"
   echo "Known regions: ${#ARRAY[@]}"
   i=0
   while [ $i -le $count ]; do
   parse_line=(`echo ${ARRAY[i]} | awk '{print $1}'`)
   echo "$parse_line\n"
   let i=i+1
   done
    exit 1
fi
 
#  capture Add or Delete from command
ADD_DELETE=`echo $1 | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`
 
#
# Interface to use:  en0 = Ethernet,  en1 = Airport,  utun0 = Anyconnect
#
MYIF=`echo $2 | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`
 
LOCAL_4=`ifconfig $MYIF | grep -E 'inet ' | grep -v '127.0.0.1' | awk '{print $2}'`
 
#  construct FQDN for router
#
FOUND=0
ISATAP_NAME=`echo $3 | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`
echo "$ISATAP_NAME" | grep -q 'isatap'
if [ $? = 0 ]; then
   # appears that the FQDN was provided
   ISATAP_NAME=`echo $3 | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`
   FOUND=1
else
   #  check for abbreviated region
   echo "$ISATAP_NAME" | grep -q '.com$'
   if [ $? != 0 ]; then
    #passed in a short name
    i=0
    while [ $i -le $count ]; do
        parse_line=(`echo ${ARRAY[i]} | awk '{print $1}' | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`)
        echo $parse_line | grep  -q $ISATAP_NAME
        if [ $? = 0 ]; then
            ISATAP_NAME="isatap.$parse_line"
            FOUND=1
            break
        fi
    let i=i+1
    done
   else
    ISATAP_NAME="isatap.$ISATAP_NAME"
    FOUND=1
   fi
fi
if [ $FOUND = 0 ]; then
   echo "No entry in conf file for router $ISATAP_NAME"
   echo "Known regions: ${ARRAY[@]}"
   exit 1
fi
 
 
#  capture 'test' command option
TESTING=`echo $4 | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`
 
# Replay command line
echo "Configuring $ADD_DELETE $MYIF $ISATAP_NAME $TESTING"
 
 
#######################################################################
# Remove tunnel
#######################################################################
if [ "$ADD_DELETE" = "del" ] || [ "$ADD_DELETE" = "delete" ] ; then
 
MY6LL=`ifconfig gif0 | grep -E 'inet6' | grep '5efe' | grep 'fe80' | awk '{print $2}'`
LOCAL_ISATAP=`ifconfig gif0 | grep -E 'inet6' | grep -v 'fe80' | awk '{print $2}'`
 
echo ""
echo "Deleting internal prefixes on gif0"
    route delete -inet6 -prefixlen 32 2001:420:: -interface gif0        # IT block ARIN
    route delete -inet6 -prefixlen 48 2001:470:d3cf:: -interface gif0    # Tech Center HE
    route delete -inet6 -prefixlen 48 2001:1af8:fe4f:: -interface gif0    # Tech Center Sixxs
    route delete -inet6 -prefixlen 32 2610:d0:: -interface gif0        # LISP BU block ARIN
echo "Deleting default route on gif0"
route delete -inet6 -prefixlen 0 default -interface gif0
echo "Disabling tunnel interface"
ifconfig gif0 down
echo "Deleting local ISATAP address " $LOCAL_ISATAP
ifconfig gif0 inet6 $LOCAL_ISATAP delete
echo "Deleting local link-local address " $MY6LL
ifconfig gif0 inet6 $MY6LL delete
echo "Removing tunnel"
ifconfig gif0 deletetunnel
echo "Clean up finished "
echo `ifconfig gif0`
exit 0
fi
 
 
#######################################################################
# If not delete, figure out what to add
#######################################################################
#
#
# set local isatap ipv6 prefix
#
#  get prefix and len from conf file array
#
 
i=0 ; FOUND=0
while [ $i -le $count ]; do
 
   parse_line=(`echo ${ARRAY[i]} | awk  '{print $1}' | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`)
 
   echo $ISATAP_NAME | grep -q $parse_line
   if [ $? = 0 ]; then
    TUNPREFIX=(`echo ${ARRAY[i]} | awk  '{print $2}' | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`)
    TUNPREFIXLEN=(`echo ${ARRAY[i]} | awk  '{print $3}' | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]'`)
    FOUND=1
    break
   fi
   let i=i+1
done
if [ $FOUND = 0 ]; then
   echo "IPv6 isatap prefix not known for router $ISATAP_NAME"
   echo "Known regions: ${ARRAY[@]}"
   exit 1
fi
 
# check syntax of prefix and length & strip extraneous if necessary
TUNPREFIX=${TUNPREFIX/%::/:}
TUNPREFIXLEN=${TUNPREFIXLEN/#\//}
 
 
# See if there is a hostfile entry
#    there can only be one per domain because I can't figure out how to deal with multiple
#
# Hostfile entry for anycast isatap.cisco.com 171.69.10.1
#
#
if [ "`grep $ISATAP_NAME /etc/hosts`" != "" ] ; then
    ISATAP_RR=HOSTS
else
# Check to see if we are on the correct network
#
    ISATAP_RR=`dig $ISATAP_NAME | grep "^$ISATAP_NAME" | awk '{print $4}'`
fi
 
if [ "$ISATAP_RR" = "CNAME" ] ; then
    ISATAP_NAME=`dig $ISATAP_NAME | grep "^$ISATAP_NAME" | awk '{print $5}'`
    ISATAP_RR=`dig $ISATAP_NAME | grep "^$ISATAP_NAME" | awk '{print $4}'`
fi
 
if [ "$ISATAP_RR" = "HOSTS" ] ; then
    if [ `cat /etc/hosts |grep "$ISATAP_NAME"|awk '{print $1}'|grep \$` != "\#" ] ; then
        REMOTE_4=`cat /etc/hosts |grep "$ISATAP_NAME"|awk '{print $1}'`
    fi
elif [ "$ISATAP_RR" = "A" ] ; then
    REMOTE_4=`dig $ISATAP_NAME | grep "^$ISATAP_NAME" | awk '{print $5}'`
else
    echo Not able to resolve name $ISATAP_NAME.
    exit 0
fi
 
 
echo "$ISATAP_RR   $REMOTE_4"
 
 
# now that we have an address, test it to see if it is local
#    any of 3 may work, only fail if all are lost
#
ISATAP_TEST=`ping -c 3 -i 2 $REMOTE_4 | grep "100"`
if [ "$ISATAP_TEST" = "100" ] ; then
    echo Not connected to the correct network.
    exit 0
fi
 
#
# Check for native first
LOCAL_NATIVE6=`ifconfig $MYIF | grep -E 'inet6' | grep -v 'fe80' | awk '{print $2}'`
 
if [ "$LOCAL_NATIVE6" != "" ] && [ "$ADD_DELETE" = "add" ] ; then
    echo $LOCAL_NATIVE6 already on the $MYIF interface.
    echo ISATAP was not configured.
    exit 0
fi
 
# Check to see if it has already been set up
TUNNEL_TEST=`ifconfig gif0 | grep -E 'inet6' | grep -v 'fe80' | awk '{print $2}'`
if [ "$TUNNEL_TEST" != "" ] && [ "$ADD_DELETE" = "add" ] ; then
    echo "--- ISATAP already configured!  gif0 address" $TUNNEL_TEST
    ping6 -c 3 2001:4860:8010::67    #  ping6 ipv6.google.com
    exit 0
fi
 
 
#  use one of the following
REMOTE_6="fe80::5efe:"$REMOTE_4"%gif0"
#REMOTE_6=$TUNPREFIX"0:5efe:"$REMOTE_4         #  this works but is semantically improper
 
# This is not needed for ISATAP, but create the LL anyway
# get int L2 & insert fffe
 
LOCAL_MACADDR=`ifconfig $MYIF | grep -E 'ether' | awk '{print $2}'`
 
LOCAL_IID=${LOCAL_MACADDR:0:2}${LOCAL_MACADDR:3:2}":"${LOCAL_MACADDR:6:2}"ff:fe"${LOCAL_MACADDR:9:2}":"${LOCAL_MACADDR:12:2}${LOCAL_MACADDR:15:2}
 
 
# Construct address to match a real ISATAP implementation
# get int L3 & prepend 0:5efe:
 
LOCAL_ISATAPIID="0:5efe:"$LOCAL_4
LOCAL_ISATAP=${TUNPREFIX}${LOCAL_ISATAPIID}
MY6LL="fe80::"$LOCAL_ISATAPIID
 
 
# Check for testing
#
if [ "$TESTING" = "test" ] ; then
echo ""
echo "Test output"
echo "Local L2" $LOCAL_MACADDR
echo "constructed IID" $LOCAL_IID
echo "Local IPv4 " $LOCAL_4 "  Remote IPv4 " $REMOTE_4
echo "Local IPv6 LL " $MY6LL "/" $TUNPREFIXLEN
echo "Local IPv6 ISATAP " $LOCAL_ISATAP
echo "Remote IPv6 " $REMOTE_6
echo ""
fi
 
#######################################################################
# Config tunnel
#######################################################################
if [ "$ADD_DELETE" = "add" ] ; then
ifconfig gif0 tunnel $LOCAL_4 $REMOTE_4
ifconfig gif0 inet6  $LOCAL_ISATAP prefixlen $TUNPREFIXLEN mtu 1400
ifconfig gif0 inet6  $MY6LL prefixlen $TUNPREFIXLEN alias
route add -inet6 -prefixlen 0 default $REMOTE_6
   if [ $MYIF = "utun0" ] ; then
    route add -inet6 -prefixlen 32 2001:420:: $REMOTE_6        # IT block ARIN
    route add -inet6 -prefixlen 48 2001:470:d3cf:: $REMOTE_6    # Tech Center HE
    route add -inet6 -prefixlen 48 2001:1af8:fe4f:: $REMOTE_6    # Tech Center Sixxs
    route add -inet6 -prefixlen 32 2610:d0:: $REMOTE_6        # LISP BU block ARIN
   fi
fi
 
echo " ifconfig to show current state"
#  show what is currently configured
echo `ifconfig gif0`
 
 
# Find test targets
#
#
TEST_TARGET_1="www.ipv6.cisco.com"
TEST_TARGET_2="ipv6.google.com"
#TEST_TARGET_3="ipv6.netflix.com"
#TEST_TARGET_4="ipv6.test-ipv6.com"
count=2         # number of sequential uncommented targets in the above list
#
#
q="TEST_TARGET_N"
i=1
while [ $i -le $count ]; do
 
TEST_TARGET_NAME=${q/%N/$i}
TEST_TARGET_NAME=${!TEST_TARGET_NAME}
 
TEST_TARGET_RR=`dig aaaa $TEST_TARGET_NAME @8.8.8.8 | grep "^$TEST_TARGET_NAME" | awk '{print $4}'`
 
if [ "$TEST_TARGET_RR" = "CNAME" ] ; then
    TEST_TARGET_NAME=`dig aaaa $TEST_TARGET_NAME @8.8.8.8 | grep "^$TEST_TARGET_NAME" | awk '{print $5}'`
    TEST_TARGET_RR=`dig aaaa $TEST_TARGET_NAME @8.8.8.8 | grep "^$TEST_TARGET_NAME" | awk '{print $4}'`
fi
 
if [ "$TEST_TARGET_RR" = "HOSTS" ] ; then
    if [ `cat /etc/hosts |grep "$TEST_TARGET_NAME"|awk '{print $1}'|grep \$` != "\#" ] ; then
        TEST_TARGET_ADDR=`cat /etc/hosts |grep "$TEST_TARGET_NAME"|awk '{print $1}'`
    fi
elif [ "$TEST_TARGET_RR" = "AAAA" ] ; then
    TEST_TARGET_ADDR=`dig aaaa $TEST_TARGET_NAME @8.8.8.8 | grep "^$TEST_TARGET_NAME" | awk '{print $5}'`
else
    echo Not able to resolve name $TEST_TARGET_NAME.
    exit 1
fi
 
# Test to see if IPv6 via isatap is working
echo  ping6 -c 3 $TEST_TARGET_NAME
ping6 -c 3 $TEST_TARGET_ADDR
 
let i=i+1
 
done
exit 0

During the period when IT is ramping up its management tools, enabling IPv6 on the desktop will be on a 'business need' basis. By default, systems managed by IT will have IPv6 disabled, but there will not be an active effort to keep them that way. If someone has a business need for IPv6 it can be enabled even on IT managed systems. That said, the IPv6 functionality itself will be handled on a community supported basis for the foreseeable future. Community support should be accessible via the mail lists:* ipv6-interest* non-standard-support-trolls * mac-trollsThe most current configuration information will be maintained at the NDCS

				1.3.1.3.2 Linux guide - http://www.saschahlusiak.de/linux/isatap.htm
ISATAP client for Linux

    See also: Setting up an ISATAP router on Linux

isatapd creates and maintains an ISATAP tunnel (rfc5214) in Linux.

It uses the in-kernel ISATAP support first introduced in linux-2.6.25. It does NOT operate the tunnel or handle any IPv6 traffic other than router solicitations and router advertisements.

This is NOT isatapd from miredo which was removed in miredo-1.1.6.
WHAT IT DOES

    Creating an ISATAP tunnel device based on an IPv4 interface
    Periodically querying and adding router addresses to the potential router list
    Periodically sending router solicitation messages to potential routers to maintain IPv6 connectivity
    Receiving and parsing router advertisements to adjust the router solicitation interval
    Trying to detect link changes and maintain the tunnel

USAGE

complete man page

Usage: isatapd [OPTIONS] [ROUTER]...
       -n --name       name of the tunnel
                       default: is0
       -l --link       tunnel link device
                       default: auto
       -m --mtu        set tunnel MTU
                       default: auto
       -t --ttl        set tunnel hoplimit.
                       default: 64
       -N --nopmtudisc disable ipv4 pmtu discovery.
                       default: pmtudisc enabled

       -r --router     set potential router.
                       default: 'isatap'.
       -i --interval   interval to perform router solicitation
                       default: auto
       -D --check-dns  interval to perform DNS resolution and
                       recreate PRL.
                       default: 3600 seconds

       -d --daemon     fork into background
       -p --pid        store pid of daemon in file
          --user       drop privileges to this user
                       default: 'nobody'

       -v --verbose    increase verbosity
       -q --quiet      decrease verbosity

       -h --help       display this message
          --version    display version

Linux configuration:
Couldn’t find the original email, instruction below show how to 
enable IPV6 over Linux machine. 

VI /etc/sysconfig/network
NETWORKING_IPV6=yes
IPV6_AUTOCONF=yes

IPV6_MTU=1280 (Optional)
IPV6_DEFAULTGW= ip –address  Default gateway (Optional)

VI /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth0:
PV6INIT=yes

If configure fix ip 
IPV6ADDR= ip-address

			1.3.2.2

		1.3.3 IPv6, give dual stack ipv6 address to a CARS machine in lab
Example: Sasha's machine, 10.56.13.62 

	Instructions: 
IPv6 addressing and routing between vlans are now available as per your request, on vlan13 and vlan52.
 
Required client side configuration: make it autoconfig. NOT dhcp.
Explanation: As opposed to IPv4, where we have manual ip config and dhcp, in IPv6 we have manual configuration and two competing technologies to assign addresses to clients:
a.       autoconfigâ€, also known as â€œstateless autoconfigâ€ or â€œstateless dhcpâ€;
b.       dhcp, also known as â€œstateful autoconfigâ€ or â€œstatefull dhcpâ€;
You should have this information in mind when you configure the client, as it can be different between operation systems.
 
Once you set this option, youre basically done.
 
When viewing the interface information in the client (e.g. â€œshow interface GigabitEthernet 0â€ in positron or â€œifconfig â€“aâ€ in linux) you may see more than one address. Dont panic
The address with the prefix fe80 is the Link-Local address. Itâ€™s good and routable within the vlan but not beyond.
The address with the prefix 2001 is the global address, which is routable between vlans. In some cases, the client may have two such addresses or more. Itâ€™s normal, and all are routable.
 
Addressing convention: 
The client will automatically get an address in the form of: 2001:420:44ff:13:ba:395c:10e7:513a. note the fifth chunk. It point the vlan  13 in this example
The default gateway for the client in a given vlan is always 2001:420:44ff:13:1 for vlan 13, and 2001:420:44ff:52:1 for vlan 52.

		2.1.2 Install from new ISO

- login via vsphere 
- Click Inventory
- RMB ip address "new virtual machine", or CTRL+N
- Choose custom 
- Define machine:
	-- Name it
	-- Choose data store
	-- Choose VM 7 & RH Linux 3 (32-bit)
	-- 2 CPUs
	-- 4G RAM
	-- 1 NIC, leave defaults
	-- SCSI, LSI logic SAS
	-- Create a new disk -> Disk size 70G
	-- 2X next
	-- In Ready to complete choose "edit VM settings before completion"
		--- In new CD/DVD Choose "Datastore ISO file" radio button then
			---- check "connect at power on"
			---- Data store ISO file -> browse -> Datastore -> choose ISO 
				Datastore1 (2) / Yosi/
			---- click machine power on

CARS Setup:
- go to console tab
- choose 1
- Setup:

		2.1.3 How to upload ISO to storage ?

			2.1.3.1 Vsphere GUI


- Go to summary tab
- RMB Datastore 
- browse -> go to or create dir
- click upload button 

			2.1.3.2 curl
curl -k -v -T <file> -u root 'https://<ESX host>/folder/<folder>/<file>?dsName=<datastore>'

For example:
curl -k -v -T acs55.iso -u root 'https://10.56.24.15/folder/semantay/acs55.iso?dsName=datastore1'

			2.1.3.3
		2.1.4 How to install from different ISO ?
- shutdown machine
- RM edit settings
- in options tab -> boot options check "force BIOS setup"
- In Hardware-> CD/DVD choose new ISO
- power up machine
- In Console tab, BIOS choose boot from DVD, F10

		2.1.5 troubleshooting

			2.1.5.1 No internet connectivity
ping fails,
nslookup fails,

possible fix: RMB machine -> edit settings -> check network adapter -> check connected

3. Installation

	3.1 Install root patch
id=__acs_5_root_patch__
		3.1.1 PFA ACS 5 RootPatch 
PFA ACS 5 RootPatch 

Please see EDCS 812808: ACS5-TroubleShooting.ppt   
-> Optional TAC-only add-on for diagnostic purposes
-> Adding Root Patch enables command shell access for super users
-> Root patch expires within a week
-> Root patch runs only from console port

Installation instructions example:

Preparations:
Please copy the root patch to a repository e.g. YourRepository

patch on my laptop: c:\work\acs\5.4\RootPatch\RootPatch.tar.gz 
Patch on FTP server: ftp://cd-acs-ftp/upload/yizaq/RootPatch.tar.gz 

<URL:/cygdrive/c/work/KB/ACS/kb_acs_5_1#r=__set_acs_ftp_repo__>

Patch Installation:
admin# app install RootPatch.tar.gz my_repo
Do you want to save the current configuration ? (yes/no) [yes] ? yes
Generating configuration...
Saved the running configuration to startup successfully

Application successfully installed
admin#exit
<<<<<<<<<< Shell refresh required 
<<<<<<<<<< relogin

IN Console:
admin# root_enable

admin# root
Enter root patch password :
Starting root bash shell ...
ade #

enter:
ade#passwd
enter password for unix

Now we have root password for ssh

Removing RootPatch: 
admin# sh application
<name>          <Description> 
acs             ACS 5.0
RootPatch       Cisco ADE Root Patch

admin# app remove RootPatch
Continue with application removal? [y/n] y
Application successfully uninstalled

admin# sh app
<name>          <Description> 
acs             ACS 5.0

admin#

	3.2

4. FAQ

	4.1 active directory, AD

		4.1.1  ACS can be put in a dedicated OU or must it be in the? 


To the question: "ACS can be put in a dedicated OU or must it be in the "Computers" OU?"
AFAIK, it's currently not possible to select a different OU for adding ACS to. It will add itself to Computers OU and can't be configured otherwise. 
I did a basic PAP/Kerberos test and it seems like ACS doesn't mind being transferred to a different OU from the default Computers OU. I must stress though that I don't recall such a use case being extensively tested and thus being "officially" supported.

	4.2 Protocols

		4.2.1  LEAP

			4.2.1.1  What Identity Stores work with LEAP?
(+ team)

Hi Ayumi,

LEAP is supported.
According to protocol details and our internal documentation any MS-CHAP capable ID store can be configured to work with LEAP. So should be same as EAP-FAST MSCHAPv2 (AD & Internal).
The omission from the user guide seems to be accidental. 

Thx,
Yosi

		4.2.2 EAP-TLS/PEAP with machine authentication, is internal ID supported?

			4.2.2.1  Emails
+Vicki & Yaniv.

Hi,

Conceptually the following should be true. However, only Vicki can verify what was actually tested and confirmed to work properly.
a. EAP-TLS
	- w/ binary comparison. AD required.
	- w/o binary comparison. AD not required.
b. EAP-FAST. AD required for PAC creation.
c. PEAP-GTC. AD not required.
D. PEAP-MSCHAP. AD required.
E. MAB use case - AD not required.

The user guide has some information on this as well - http://www.cisco.com/en/US/docs/net_mgmt/cisco_secure_access_control_system/5.3/user/guide/eap_pap_phase_ps9911_TSD_Products_User_Guide_Chapter.html#wp1014889

Thanks,
Yosi

Natsuko Ohno (nohno) wrote:
Hi Kemal-san and Yosi-san,
Thank you so much for your support.
It will be appreciated if I can confirm the spec of machine authentication with those protocol on ACS 5.x.
 
In the case of EAP-FAST, my partner met the problem by using internal DB.
Following communication shows AD is must to use for that.
And TAC engineer answered to my partner machine authentication with EAP-FAST must to use AD.
 
********************
http://topic.cisco.com/news/cisco/eng/cse-dev-acs5/msg15397.html
For machine PAC refresh the PC must do windows machine authentication. The PC 
 can do machine authentication only against AD.
The PC sends credentials to ACS and ACS send to AD , then AD reply to ACS. If 
authentication passed ACS sends the new machine PAC to the PC.
Hence, ACS must be joined to AD.

			4.3.1.2

		4.3.2

	4.4 Cryptography

		4.4.1 CRL

			4.4.1.1 Can ACS fetch CRLs from multiple CRLDP URLs, one per CA issuing server?

Yes. ACS supports the configuration of one static CRLDP URL per CA. It doesn't support parsing of CRL URL from the certificate
			4.4.1.2 Does ACS fetch CRLs from all CRLDP URLs in the trust chain?
Yes. ACS will also check revoke status in all the chain's CRLs

			4.4.1.3 "Bypass CRL Verification if CRL is not Received", would it fail when not able to fetch CRL but a valid CRL is in cache?

No. The valid CRL in cache will be used

Another Q:
"there was a question that came up during the CPOC that I could not find an answer for. It is around the handling of CRLs.
On ACS, there is a checkmark on the CRL Part that says something like "bypass CRL verification if download fails". Default is unchecked, so if the download fails, ACS is expected to fail authentications because it can't download the new CRL.
 
Now the question is; When does it actually start failing Authentications? Directly after it fails to download the CRL, or after then CRL expiration when at the same time ACS is not able to download the CRL?
"
A:
Code in CRLManager that has a d/l worker thread member of type CRLHttpWorker()
in svc() (work code) treatment of fail to d/l is:
    			bool res = download(data, crlData, resultMsg);
    
    			do //parse and set the next download
    			{
                    std::auto_ptr<Context> pCtx( new Context());
                    if( pCtx.get()==NULL )
                        break ;;

                    pCtx->setAsString (ConfigAttributeSetType::REQUEST, Acs::CrlUrl, data->m_urlData.m_url);
                    if(!res)
    				{
    					data->m_nextUpdate = ACE_OS::gettimeofday() 
    								+ ACE_Time_Value(data->m_urlData.m_downloadFailureRetires);
    
                        pCtx->setAsString( ConfigAttributeSetType::REQUEST, Acs::LastErrorMessage, resultMsg ) ;
    
                        ACS_LOG_DEBUG(m_log) << "Failed to download CRL with error: " << resultMsg ;
    
                        (void)NotificationCenter::log  (MessageCatalog::CRL_DOWLOAD_ERROR, pCtx.get(), "CryptoLib");
    					break;
    				}

So, no failure flag and no delete CRL from cache!

Official answer:
According to the source code the answer is - ACS actually start failing authentications when a - CRL has expired and b- ACS is not able to download a valid CRL.
I don't know about test coverage of this area by QA but save for a possible bug this is how ACS should behave.



			4.4.1.4 where is CRL download reported?

Can you please tell me the exact report in which they are presented?

			4.4.1.6
		4.4.2 SFTP


			4.4.2.1 SFTP: Is the password only required even with the host – key sync ? ie” we can remove this command after the host key sync process command is completed ?
 
Or is username and password still required after the host – key sync occurs ?
Hello Michael

ACS is generating a public/private key pair during the installation.
These keys and are used to open SSL tunnels with SSH and SFTP servers.
ACS needs the public key of the SSH or the SFTP server in order to encrypt the data within the SSL tunnel.
“host-key sync” makes ACS to exchange the public keys with the SSH or the SFTP server.
ACS as an SSH client or SFTP client may cache the public key of the SSH servers or the SFTP servers as a mean of authenticating the server. 
ACS user is prompted to approve the public key of the SSH or the SFTP server.
If the ACS user approves, then the public key of the SSH or the SFTP server is cached, and ACS will not ask again the ACS user to approve it.

Thanks 
Isaac Peleg 
From: Michael Peeters (mpeeters) 
Sent: Thursday, March 15, 2012 12:01 AM

			4.4.2.2
		4.4.3 EAP- TLS


			4.4.3.1  What RFC version is supported?
see emails:
Yes. The question is, does the customer specifically need new features added to 2716. Namely one, or more of (list of changes - taken from RFC):
“
o  As EAP is now in use with a variety of lower layers, not just PPP
      for which it was first designed, mention of PPP is restricted to
      situations relating to PPP-specific behavior and reference is made
      to other lower layers such as IEEE 802.11, IEEE 802.16, etc.

   o  The document now cites TLS v1.1 as a normative reference (Sections
      1 and 6.1).

   o  The terminology section has been updated to reflect definitions
      from [RFC3748] (Section 1.2), and the EAP Key Management Framework
      [KEYFRAME] (Section 1.2).

   o  Use for peer unauthenticated access is clarified (Section 2.1.1).

   o  Privacy is supported as an optional feature (Section 2.1.4).

   o  It is no longer recommended that the identity presented in the
      EAP-Response/Identity be compared to the identity provided in the
      peer certificate (Section 2.2).

   o  The EAP-TLS key hierarchy is defined, using terminology from
      [RFC3748].  This includes formulas for the computation of TEKs as
      well as the MSK, EMSK, IV, and Session-Id (Section 2.3).

   o  Mandatory and recommended TLS ciphersuites are provided.  The use
      of TLS ciphersuite negotiation for determining the lower layer
      ciphersuite is prohibited (Section 2.4).

   o  The Start bit is not set within an EAP-Response packet (Section
      3.2).

   o  A section on security claims has been added and advice on key
      strength is provided (Section 5.1).

   o  The Peer-Id and Server-Id are defined (Section 5.2), and
      requirements for certificate validation (Section 5.3) and
      revocation (Section 5.4) are provided.

   o  Packet modification attacks are described (Section 5.5).
“

This list needs to be distilled into “real” new features (as opposed to recommendations, explanations or change of terminology). 

Thx,
Yosi


From: Sergey Emantayev (semantay) 
Sent: Tuesday, May 29, 2012 11:17 AM
To: Kemal Akozer (kemal)
Cc: Yosi Izaq (yizaq); Yaniv Azoulay (yazoulay); Alexander Shabanov (ashabano); Oleg Pekar (olpekar)
Subject: Re: Discuss Open Cases - Client Services (Lawrence)

Hi Kemal,

We support an older EAP-TLS RFC 2716. For example, new features like TLS 1.1 are not supported.

Thanks,
Sergey

You have new mail in /var/spool/mail/root

     25      25    1613

- 5.4 MSFS
CiscoSSL
ACS 5.4 employs a new SSL library CiscoSSL due to a number of requirements:
"	PKI name constraints extension support
"	EAP-TLS session ticket extension support (stateless session resumption)

CiscoSSL is based on OpenSSL 9.8.r and provides the above-mentioned features.

The suggested tests should include full regression on all TLS based protocols (EAP-TLS, EAP-FAST, PEAP) and all PKI use cases.

	4.6 Upgrade


		4.6.1  Application Upgrade CLI

			4.6.1.1 Manifest file not found in the bundle, storeddata partition too small

- summary
-- clean storeddata partition
[root@acs-yizaq-01 ~]# df -h /storeddata/
Filesystem            Size  Used Avail Use% Mounted on
/dev/mapper/smosvg-storeddatavol
                      4.9G  4.7G   25M 100% /storeddata
[root@acs-yizaq-01 ~]# rm -fr !$/*
rm -fr /storeddata//*

*/

-- extend partition
  lvextend -L5G /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; umount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; e2fsck -f /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; resize2fs /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; mount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol


- email
Hi Yosi,

Basically the root cause is that less than 500gb server will gave only 2gb of /storeddata partition size which is not sufficient for upgrading 5.4.

If it is for our purpose you could increase the size by running below commands,

  lvextend -L5G /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol
  umount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol
  e2fsck -f /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol
  resize2fs /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol
  mount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol

  lvextend -L5G /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; umount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; e2fsck -f /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; resize2fs /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol; mount /dev/smosvg/storeddatavol

Thanks,
Satheesh kumar.

From: Satheesh kumar [mailto:satmurug@cisco.com] 
Sent: Thursday, May 10, 2012 3:14 PM
To: 'Yosi Izaq (yizaq)'; 'Sivaraja Krishnamoorthy -X (sikrishn - HCL TECHNOLOGIES LIMITED at Cisco)'; 'Yaniv Azoulay (yazoulay)'; 'Sergey Emantayev (semantay)'; 'Premanand Seralathan -X (pseralat - HCL TECHNOLOGIES LIMITED at Cisco)'
Cc: 'Alexander Shabanov (ashabano)'; 'Alon Barak (albarak)'
Subject: RE: bugs after app upgrade acs.tar.gz 

Hi Yosi,

I could see that you are trying to upgrade a server which has less than 500gb hard disk space. As you may aware, it is a unsupported setup for upgrading from ACS 5.3 to ACS 5.4. We know this earlier and documented it We like to reiterate that customer should go through upgrade documentation before they are going for it.

We understand that this error message is wrong , But this message is thrown from the 5.3 CARS code so any change we make now may not help for ACS 5.3.  but we are tracking issues like this and will fix those keeping in mind ACS 5.5.

Thanks,
Satheesh kumar.

		4.9.2

	4.10 Administration


		4.10.1  NTP

			4.10.1.1  NTP - Does ACS 5.3 for VM support both Slew or Step mode? 
Hi Norikazu,

Response inline:
“
1. Does ACS 5.3 for VM support both Slew or Step mode? 
*Step is one time correction method while Slew is a gradual correction method for NTP time adjustment. 
[Yosi] ACS supports both options, though currently, to the best of my knowledge & checks, the -x flag (no step) is not exposed to the admin.
So NTPD intrinsic algorithm + real time conditions dictate which mod is actually used.

2. If both Slew or Step mode is supported, could you please tell me the condition when to use slew and step mode? 
As with Unix OS, NTP time adjustment is based on the below rules. Does ACS 5.3 for VM follow the same rules or not? 
----
If less than 128msec of time difference, Slew method is used to correct the time in the switch. 
If more than 128msec of time difference, Step method is used. 
---- 
[Yosi] Yes, the manual and anecdotal evidence that I've encountered suggests that it's so, *but* this was not thoroughly tested in our labs.

3. If the above rules is applied to ACS, can we configure the msec value? If it's possible, could you please let me know the minimum and maximum value.
[Yosi] Not possible. This configuration is not exposed to the admin. 
 
4. Does ACS 5.3 has following functions?
- The configurable values to sync the time with the upper NTP server which ntpd terminates automatically
[Yosi] Please specify the values. 
- Operate ntpdate before ntpd is running
[Yosi] To that I've added Eddie & Isaac. I saw in our debug logs that at some conditions ntpdate runs prior to ntpd. Perhaps Eddie will know more re. the specifics. 
- Detection of synchronization error with the NTP server
[Yosi] AFAIK Not reported to the admin
- Detection of connection error with the NTP server
[Yosi] AFAIK Not reported to the admin. Basically, the admin can only get this and the above info. manually by using the sh ntp CLI
“

Thanks,
Yosi

10. Interesting Customer cases

	10.1 Active-Directory

		10.1.1 Subject: RE: [#3757] New Issue: ACS_5x Case: SR 622139921 ACS 5.3 Group retrieval from trusted domains HANNA BROPHY MACLEAN Medium (Sev3)
Hi Igal,

Please, follow my recommendations as we already discussed 

Please, perform conference call with the customer and perform the following steps (please follow the order strictly; do not perform authentications until step 8):
|1.	Install ACS 5.3 patch 5.
|2.	Stop ACS services
|3.	Run from root console:
/opt/CSCOacs/runtime/adagent/bin/ACS_AD_Runner.sh adflush –f
|4.	Start ACS services
|5.	Wait 2 minutes (adclients need to gather/rebuild data about forests/domains/etc. because we flushed the cache)
|6.	Switch adagent debug log on.
|7.	Configure ‘adclient.find.domain.local.groups’ to true. Use command – do not edit centrifydc.conf manually (Pay attention this command restarts adclient).
1) Inter to acs config mode:  acs-config
2) Insert :  ad-agent-configuration adclient.find.domain.local.groups true
3) Choose: ‘y’
|8.	Perform test authentications. 
|9.	If the problem persist (sec.lab/Users/Big Group is still not here as the customer expects) then please gather support bundle with debug logs.
|10.	If the problem persist additionally verify with the customer:
a.	Which type is ‘Big Group’ group? (We suspect domain local but double check.)
b.	How is user from syd.aaa included in this group (Directly? Indirectly? Via which group? (What type? Where located?))?
c.	Are sec.lab and syd.aaa two forests or two domains in the same forest?

Thanks,
Sasha

Hi Chris,
 
This was my scenario, per TAC description:
 
Igal’s test:
“I did a test in my lab:
Domain functional level Windows 2003. 
Forest functional level 2000 mixed, and Windows 2003.
 
ACS --> september.local --> october.local  (two way trust).
User 'Toto' exists in October.local , member of global group 'totoGlobalGroup' that exists in october.local 'totoGlobalGroup' member of 'totoLocalGroup' that exists in September.local.
 
Authentication works fine, with ACS 5.3 patch 5. ACS can fetch 'totoLocalGroup' . AccessAccept is depends on membership in 'totoLocalGroup'”
 
TAC’s test:
“> *ACS 5.3 (no patches) is connected to the "sec.lab" domain *The sec.lab domain has a two way trust with syd.aaa
> 
> ACS ----> sec.lab ----> syd.aaa
> 
> *User "iamsecond" exists in syd.aaa
> *Group "Big Group" exists in sec.lab
> *The user iamsecond is a member of Big Group
> 
> Here is what I did:
> *I ran a test authentication with user "iamsecond". Group membership was successfully retrieved for this user:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Users/Big Group *The customer is running 5.3 with patch 4 and is seeing problems with group retrieval, so I went through the very fun process of trying each one of the patches (from 1 to 5) and the results are as follows:
> I see the expected group information retrieved with no patches, patch 1 and patch 2:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Users/Big Group
> 
> Patch 3, patch 4 and patch 5 return this:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Builtin/Users
> 
> 
> So something has happened in patch 3 where this functionality is no longer available. This behaviour that we see in patches 3, 4 and 5 is the same as what we were seeing for my customer in SR 619029597 while he was running ACS 5.2 patch 6.
“
 
 
 
 
Thanks,
Igal.

>      Hi team,
> 
> I'm working with a customer that is seeing problems with group retrieval from the trusted domain. I am still working with the customer to clarify exactly what they're seeing, but I did carry out some test in the lab and have found something interesting.
> 
> I have worked previously with Chris Murray on the same issue (SR 619029597), so if he is able to help out here again that would be great.
> 
> I'll explain what I have in our lab:
> *ACS 5.3 (no patches) is connected to the "sec.lab" domain *The sec.lab domain has a two way trust with syd.aaa
> 
> ACS ----> sec.lab ----> syd.aaa
> 
> *User "iamsecond" exists in syd.aaa
> *Group "Big Group" exists in sec.lab
> *The user iamsecond is a member of Big Group
> 
> Here is what I did:
> *I ran a test authentication with user "iamsecond". Group membership was successfully retrieved for this user:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Users/Big Group *The customer is running 5.3 with patch 4 and is seeing problems with group retrieval, so I went through the very fun process of trying each one of the patches (from 1 to 5) and the results are as follows:
> I see the expected group information retrieved with no patches, patch 1 and patch 2:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Users/Big Group
> 
> Patch 3, patch 4 and patch 5 return this:
> ExternalGroups=syd.aaa/Users/Domain Users ExternalGroups=sec.lab/Builtin/Users
> 
> 
> So something has happened in patch 3 where this functionality is no longer available. This behaviour that we see in patches 3, 4 and 5 is the same as what we were seeing for my customer in SR 619029597 while he was running ACS 5.2 patch 6.
> 
> While working with Chris on 619029597, he explained that this was a bug in Centrify 4.3 and that is was fixed in Centrify 4.5 (ACS 5.3 no patches was where this fix was included). All my email exchanges with Chris in regards to SR 619029597 have been copied to the case notes.
> 
> So, my questions are:
> 1. Was this functionality removed on purpose?
> 2. When can we expect to get it back?
> 
> Thank you in advance,
> Dragana
